      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Agriculture">Agriculture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Agriculture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The majority of Guineans work in the agriculture sector, which employs approximately 75% of the country. The rice is cultivated in the flooded zones between streams and rivers. However, the local production of rice is not sufficient to feed the country, so rice is imported from Asia. The <a href="/wiki/Agriculture_in_Guinea" title="Agriculture in Guinea">agriculture sector of Guinea</a> cultivates coffee beans, pineapples, peaches, nectarines, <a href="/wiki/Mango" title="Mango">mangoes</a>, oranges, bananas, potatoes, tomatoes, cucumbers, pepper, and many other types of produce. Guinea is one of the emerging regional producers of apples and pears. There are many plantations of grapes, pomegranates, and recent years have seen the development of strawberry plantations based on the vertical hydroponic system. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Le_%22Voile%22_de_la_mari%C3%A9e_%C3%A0_Kindia.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Le_%22Voile%22_de_la_mari%C3%A9e_%C3%A0_Kindia.png/220px-Le_%22Voile%22_de_la_mari%C3%A9e_%C3%A0_Kindia.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="232" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Le_%22Voile%22_de_la_mari%C3%A9e_%C3%A0_Kindia.png/330px-Le_%22Voile%22_de_la_mari%C3%A9e_%C3%A0_Kindia.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Le_%22Voile%22_de_la_mari%C3%A9e_%C3%A0_Kindia.png/440px-Le_%22Voile%22_de_la_mari%C3%A9e_%C3%A0_Kindia.png 2x" data-file-width="979" data-file-height="1033"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Le_%22Voile%22_de_la_mari%C3%A9e_%C3%A0_Kindia.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Le "Voile" de la mari√©e √† Kindia
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Due to its diverse geography, Guinea presents some interesting tourist sites. Among the top attractions are the waterfalls found mostly in the Basse Guinee (Lower Guinea) and Moyenne Guinee (Middle Guinea) regions. The Soumba cascade at the foot of Mount Kakoulima in Kindia, Voile de la Mari√©e (bride's veil) in Dubreka, the Kinkon cascades that are about 80&nbsp;m (260&nbsp;ft) high on the Kokoula River in the prefecture of Pita, the Kambadaga falls that can reach 100&nbsp;m (330&nbsp;ft) during the rainy season on the same river, the Ditinn &amp; Mitty waterfalls in Dalaba, and the Fetor√© waterfalls and the stone bridge in the region of Labe are among the most well-known water-related tourist sites. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Problems_and_reforms">Problems and reforms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Problems and reforms">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>In 2002, the <a href="/wiki/IMF" class="mw-redirect" title="IMF">IMF</a> suspended Guinea's <a href="/wiki/Poverty_Reduction_and_Growth_Facility" title="Poverty Reduction and Growth Facility">Poverty Reduction and Growth Facility</a> (PRGF) because the government failed to meet key performance criteria. In reviews of the PRGF, the World Bank noted that Guinea had met its spending goals in targeted social priority sectors. However, spending in other areas, primarily defense, contributed to a significant fiscal deficit.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> The loss of IMF funds forced the government to finance its debts through <a href="/wiki/Central_Bank" class="mw-redirect" title="Central Bank">Central Bank</a> advances. The pursuit of unsound economic policies has resulted in imbalances that are proving hard to correct. </p>
      <p>Under then-Prime Minister Diallo, the government began a rigorous reform agenda in December 2004 designed to return Guinea to a PRGF with the IMF. Exchange rates have been allowed to float, price controls on gasoline have been loosened, and government spending has been reduced while tax collection has been improved. These reforms have not reduced inflation, which hit 27% in 2004 and 30% in 2005. <a href="/wiki/Currency_depreciation" class="mw-redirect" title="Currency depreciation">Currency depreciation</a> is also a concern. The Guinea franc was trading at 2550 to the dollar in January 2005. It hit 5554 to the dollar by October 2006. In August 2016 that number had reached 9089. </p>
      <p>Despite the opening in 2005 of a new road connecting Guinea and Mali, most major roadways remain in poor repair, slowing the delivery of goods to local markets. Electricity and water shortages are frequent and sustained, and many businesses are forced to use expensive power generators and fuel to stay open. </p>
      <p>Even though there are many problems plaguing Guinea's economy, not all foreign investors are reluctant to come to Guinea. Global Alumina's proposed alumina refinery has a price tag above $2&nbsp;billion. Alcoa and Alcan are proposing a slightly smaller refinery worth about $1.5&nbsp;billion. Taken together, they represent the largest private investment in <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africa" title="Sub-Saharan Africa">sub-Saharan Africa</a> since the <a href="/wiki/Chad-Cameroon_Petroleum_Development_and_Pipeline_Project" class="mw-redirect" title="Chad-Cameroon Petroleum Development and Pipeline Project">Chad-Cameroon oil pipeline</a>. Also, Hyperdynamics Corporation, an American oil company, signed an agreement in 2006 to develop Guinea's offshore <a href="/wiki/Senegal_River" title="Senegal River">Senegal Basin</a> oil deposits in a concession of 31,000 square miles (80,000&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup>); it is pursuing seismic exploration.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 13 October 2009, Guinean Mines Minister Mahmoud Thiam announced that the <a href="/wiki/China_International_Fund" title="China International Fund">China International Fund</a> would invest more than $7bn (¬£4.5bn) in infrastructure. In return, he said the firm would be a "strategic partner" in all mining projects in the mineral-rich nation. He said the firm would help build ports, railway lines, power plants, low-cost housing and even a new administrative centre in the capital, <a href="/wiki/Conakry" title="Conakry">Conakry</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> In September 2011, Mohamed Lamine Fofana, the Mines Minister following the <a href="/wiki/Guinean_presidential_election,_2010" class="mw-redirect" title="Guinean presidential election, 2010">2010 election</a>, said that the government had overturned the agreement by the ex-military junta.<sup id="cite_ref-bbcmines_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbcmines-73">[73]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Youth unemployment remains a large problem. Guinea needs an adequate policy to address the concerns of urban youth. One problem is the disparity between their life and what they see on television. For youth who cannot find jobs, seeing the economic power and consumerism of richer countries only serves to frustrate them further.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mining_controversies">Mining controversies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Mining controversies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Guinea has large reserves of the steel-making raw material, iron ore. <a href="/wiki/Rio_Tinto_Group" class="mw-redirect" title="Rio Tinto Group">Rio Tinto Group</a> was the majority owner of the $6&nbsp;billion <a href="/wiki/Simandou" title="Simandou">Simandou</a> iron ore project, which it had called the world's best unexploited resource. This project is said to be of the same magnitude as the <a href="/wiki/Pilbara" title="Pilbara">Pilbara</a> in Western Australia.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2017, <a href="/wiki/Och-Ziff_Capital_Management_Group" class="mw-redirect" title="Och-Ziff Capital Management Group">Och-Ziff Capital Management Group</a> pled guilty to a multi-year bribery scheme, after an investigation by the <a href="/wiki/Securities_and_Exchange_Commission" class="mw-redirect" title="Securities and Exchange Commission">Securities and Exchange Commission</a> (SEC) led to a trial in the United States and a fine of $412&nbsp;million.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> Following this, the SEC also filed a lawsuit in the US against head of Och-Ziff European operations, Michael Cohen,<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> for his role in a bribery scheme in the region.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2009 the government of Guinea gave the northern half of Simandou to BSGR<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> for an $165&nbsp;million investment in the project and a pledge to spend $1&nbsp;billion on railways, saying that Rio Tinto wasn't moving into production fast enough. The US Justice Department investigated allegations that BSGR had bribed President Cont√©'s wife to get him the concession,<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> and so did the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Bureau_of_Investigation" title="Federal Bureau of Investigation">Federal Bureau of Investigation</a>, the next elected President of Guinea, <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Cond%C3%A9" title="Alpha Cond√©">Alpha Cond√©</a>, and an assortment of other national and international entities. </p>
      <p>In April 2014 the Guinean government cancelled the company's mining rights in Simandou. BSGR has denied any wrongdoing, and in May 2014 sought arbitration over the government of Guinea's decision to expropriate its mining rights.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> In February 2019, <a href="/wiki/BSG_Resources" class="mw-redirect" title="BSG Resources">BSGR</a> and Guinean President <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Cond%C3%A9" title="Alpha Cond√©">Alpha Cond√©</a> agreed to drop all <a href="/wiki/Allegation" title="Allegation">allegations</a> of wrongdoing as well as the pending <a href="/wiki/Arbitration" title="Arbitration">arbitration</a> case.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> Under the agreement, BSGR would relinquish rights to <a href="/wiki/Simandou" title="Simandou">Simandou</a> while being allowed to maintain an interest in the smaller <a href="/wiki/Zogota" title="Zogota">Zogota</a> deposit that would be developed by Niron Metals head <a href="/wiki/Mick_Davis" title="Mick Davis">Mick Davis</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2010 Rio Tinto signed a binding agreement with <a href="/wiki/Aluminum_Corporation_of_China_Limited" title="Aluminum Corporation of China Limited">Aluminum Corporation of China Limited</a> to establish a joint venture for the Simandou iron ore project.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> In November 2016, Rio Tinto admitted paying $10.5&nbsp;million to a close adviser of President Alpha Cond√© to obtain rights on Simandou.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> Conde said he knew nothing about the bribe and denied any wrongdoing. However, according to recordings obtained by <a href="/wiki/FRANCE_24" class="mw-redirect" title="FRANCE 24">FRANCE 24</a>, Guinean authorities were aware of the Simandou briberies.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In July 2017, the UK-based anti-fraud regulator, the <a href="/wiki/Serious_Fraud_Office_(United_Kingdom)" title="Serious Fraud Office (United Kingdom)">Serious Fraud Office</a> (SFO) and the <a href="/wiki/Australian_Federal_Police" title="Australian Federal Police">Australian Federal Police</a><sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> launched an investigation into Rio Tinto's business practices in Guinea.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Further, In November 2016, the former mining minister of Guinea, Mahmoud Thiam, accused head of Rio Tinto's Guinea operation department of offering him a bribe in 2010 to regain Rio Tinto's control over half of the undeveloped Simandou project. </p>
      <p>In September 2011, Guinea adopted a new mining code. The law set up a commission to review government deals struck during the chaotic days between the end of dictatorship in 2008 and Cond√© coming to power.<sup id="cite_ref-TST_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TST-93">[93]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In September 2015, the French Financial Public Prosecutor's Office launched an investigation into President Alpha Conde's son, Mohamed Alpha Cond√©.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> He was charged with embezzlement of public funds and receiving financial and other benefits from French companies that were interested in the Guinean mining industry.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In August 2016, son of a former Prime Minister of Gabon, who worked for Och-Ziff's Africa Management Ltd, a subsidiary of the U.S. hedge fund Och-Ziff, was arrested in the US and charged with bribing officials in Guinea, Chad and Niger on behalf of the company to secure mining concessions<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> and gain access to relevant confidential information.<sup id="cite_ref-justice.gov_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-justice.gov-98">[98]</a></sup> The investigation also revealed that he was involved in rewriting Guinea's mining law during President Conde's rule.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> In December 2016, the US Department of Justice announced that the man pleaded guilty to conspiring to make corrupt payments to government officials in Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-justice.gov_98-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-justice.gov-98">[98]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>According to a Global Witness report, Sable Mining sought iron ore explorations rights to Mount Nimba in Guinea by getting close to Conde towards the 2010 elections, backing his campaign for presidency and bribing his son.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> These allegations have not been verified yet but in March 2016 Guinean authorities ordered an investigation into the matter.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Conde government investigated two other contracts as well, one which left Hyperdynamic with a third of Guinea's offshore lease allocations as well as <a href="/wiki/Rusal" title="Rusal">Rusal</a>'s purchase of the Friguia Aluminum refinery, in which it said that Rusal greatly underpaid.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span id="Minority_and_women.27s_rights"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Minority_and_women's_rights">Minority and women's rights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Minority and women's rights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Guinea" title="Human rights in Guinea">Human rights in Guinea</a>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_Guinea" title="LGBT rights in Guinea">Homosexuality</a> is illegal in Guinea.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> Same sex relations are considered a strong taboo, and the prime minister declared in 2010 that he doesn't consider sexual orientation a legitimate human right.<sup id="cite_ref-State_2011_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-State_2011-18">[18]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Guinea has one of the world's highest rates of <a href="/wiki/Female_genital_mutilation" title="Female genital mutilation">female genital mutilation</a> according to Anastasia Gage, an associate professor at <a href="/wiki/Tulane_University" title="Tulane University">Tulane University</a>, and Ronan van Rossem, an associate professor at <a href="/wiki/Ghent_University" title="Ghent University">Ghent University</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> Female genital mutilation in Guinea had been performed on more than 98% of women as of 2009<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Guinea&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>.<sup id="cite_ref-The_effects_of_female_genital_mutil_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_effects_of_female_genital_mutil-105">[105]</a></sup> In Guinea almost all cultures, religions, and ethnicities practice female genital mutilation.<sup id="cite_ref-The_effects_of_female_genital_mutil_105-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_effects_of_female_genital_mutil-105">[105]</a></sup> The 2005 <a href="/wiki/Demographic_and_Health_Survey" class="mw-redirect" title="Demographic and Health Survey">Demographic and Health Survey</a> reported that 96% of women have gone through the operation. Prosecutions of its practitioners are nonexistent.<sup id="cite_ref-State_2011_18-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-State_2011-18">[18]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport_infrastructure">Transport infrastructure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Transport infrastructure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Guinea" title="Transport in Guinea">Transport in Guinea</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span id="Air_.26_River"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Air_&amp;_River">Air &amp; River</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Air &amp; River">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Conakry_International_Airport" title="Conakry International Airport">Conakry International Airport</a> is the largest airport in the country, with flights to other cities in Africa as well as to Europe. Domestic air services are intermittent. There is some river traffic on the <a href="/wiki/Niger_River" title="Niger River">Niger</a> and <a href="/wiki/Milo_River" title="Milo River">Milo</a> rivers. </p>
      <p><br> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Railways">Railways</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Railways">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Built between 1904 and 1910, a railway once linked Conakry to <a href="/wiki/Kankan" title="Kankan">Kankan</a> via <a href="/wiki/Kouroussa" title="Kouroussa">Kouroussa</a> but it ceased operating in 1995<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> and had been dismantled altogether by 2007 with rails mostly stolen and/or sold for scrap. Plans had at one time been mooted for the passenger line to be rehabilitated as part of an iron-ore development masterplan but although the start of work was announced in 2010, corruption charges led the whole masterplan to be paused and the line was only rebuilt as a 105km mineral railway, paralleling the old route as far as the mines of <a href="/wiki/Kalia,_Faranah" title="Kalia, Faranah">Kalia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> There is also a state run mineral railway linking the bauxite mines of <a href="/wiki/Sangar%C3%A9di" title="Sangar√©di">Sangar√©di</a> to the port of <a href="/wiki/Kamsar" title="Kamsar">Kamsar</a> (137km) and a 1960s narrow-gauge line operated by Russian aluminium producer <a href="/wiki/RusAl" class="mw-redirect" title="RusAl">RusAl</a> to the mines at <a href="/wiki/Fria" title="Fria">Fria</a> (143km). </p>
      <p>As part of the plans to re-start iron ore mining at <a href="/wiki/Simandou" title="Simandou">Simandou</a> blocks 1 and 2, the new development consortium pledged in 2019 to fund the construction of a new heavy-duty <a href="/wiki/Standard_gauge" class="mw-redirect" title="Standard gauge">standard gauge</a> railway to <a href="/wiki/Matakong" title="Matakong">Matakong</a> on the Atlantic coast where they would also invest some US$20 billion in developing a deepwater port.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> The 650km route is far longer than an alternative heading south to the port of <a href="/wiki/Buchanan,_Liberia" title="Buchanan, Liberia">Buchanan, Liberia</a>, which was considered as an alternative in an October 2019 feasibility study.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> However, the Matakong route would be entirely within Guinea and tied to an agrigultural development corridor for citizens along the route. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Road_Transport">Road Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Road Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Most vehicles in Guinea are 20+ years old, and cabs are any four-door vehicle which the owner has designated as being for hire. Locals, nearly entirely without vehicles of their own, rely upon these taxis (which charge per seat) and small buses to take them around town and across the country. The major roads of Guinea are the following: </p> 
      <ul>
       <li>N1 connects Conakry, Coyah, Kindia, Mamou, Dabola, Kouroussa, and Kankan.</li> 
       <li>N2 connects Mamou, Faranah, Kissidougou, Gu√©k√©dou, Macenta, Nz√©r√©kor√©, and Lola.</li> 
       <li>N4 connects Coyah, For√©cariah, and, Farmoreya.</li> 
       <li>N5 connects Mamou, Dalaba, Pita, and Lab√©.</li> 
       <li>N6 connects Kissidougou, Kankan, and Siguiri.</li> 
       <li>N20 connects Kamsar, Kolaboui, and Bok√©.</li>
      </ul> 
      <p>Horses and donkeys pull carts, primarily to transport construction materials. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demography">Demography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Demography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <table class="wikitable" style="float: right; margin-left: 10px"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <th colspan="4" style="text-align:center; background:#cfb;">Population in Guinea<sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-2">[2]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_2019_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP_2019-3">[3]</a></sup> </th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <th style="background:#cfb;">Year </th> 
         <th style="background:#cfb;">Million </th>

        <tr> 
         <td style="text-align:left;">1950</td> 
         <td style="text-align:right;">3.0 </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td style="text-align:left;">2000</td> 
         <td style="text-align:right;">8.8 </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td style="text-align:left;">2018</td> 
         <td style="text-align:right;">12.4 </td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demography_of_Guinea" class="mw-redirect" title="Demography of Guinea">Demography of Guinea</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The population of Guinea is estimated at 12.4&nbsp;million. <a href="/wiki/Conakry" title="Conakry">Conakry</a>, the capital and largest city, is the hub of Guinea's economy, commerce, education, and culture. In 2014, the <a href="/wiki/Total_fertility_rate" title="Total fertility rate">total fertility rate</a> (TFR) of Guinea was estimated at 4.93 children born per woman.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Urbanization">Urbanization</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Urbanization">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Guinea" title="Languages of Guinea">Languages of Guinea</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Pita,_Guinea.gif" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Pita%2C_Guinea.gif/200px-Pita%2C_Guinea.gif" decoding="async" width="200" height="302" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Pita%2C_Guinea.gif/300px-Pita%2C_Guinea.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/9e/Pita%2C_Guinea.gif 2x" data-file-width="398" data-file-height="600"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Pita,_Guinea.gif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Guinean women
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The official language of Guinea is <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>. <a href="/wiki/Fula_language" title="Fula language">Pulaar</a> was spoken by 33.9% of the population in 2018 as their first or native language. Followed by <a href="/wiki/Mandinka_language" title="Mandinka language">Mandinka language</a>, which was spoken by 29.4% of the population in 2018 as their first language. The third most spoken native language is the <a href="/wiki/Susu_language" title="Susu language">Susu language</a>, which was spoken by 21.2% of the population in 2018 as their first language. Other languages spoken in Guinea include <a href="/wiki/Kissi_language" title="Kissi language">Kissi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kpelle_language" title="Kpelle language">Kpelle</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Guinea" title="Languages of Guinea">other languages</a>, which were spoken by 16% of the population altogether in 2018 as their native languages.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_Factbook_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_Factbook-112">[112]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnic_groups">Ethnic groups</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Ethnic groups">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The population of Guinea comprises about 24 ethnic groups. The <a href="/wiki/Mandinka_people" title="Mandinka people">Mandinka</a>, also known as Mandingo or Malink√©, comprise 29.4%<sup id="cite_ref-cia.gov_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia.gov-113">[113]</a></sup> of the population and are mostly found in eastern Guinea concentrated around the <a href="/wiki/Kankan_Prefecture" title="Kankan Prefecture">Kankan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kissidougou_Prefecture" title="Kissidougou Prefecture">Kissidougou</a> prefectures.<sup id="cite_ref-guinea_stats_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guinea_stats-12">[12]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Fula_people" title="Fula people">Fulas or Fulani</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Fula_52-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fula-52">[52]</a></sup> comprise 33.4%<sup id="cite_ref-cia.gov_113-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia.gov-113">[113]</a></sup> of the population and are mostly found in the <a href="/wiki/Futa_Djallon" class="mw-redirect" title="Futa Djallon">Futa Djallon</a> region. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Soussou" class="mw-redirect" title="Soussou">Soussou</a>, comprising 21.2% of the population, are predominantly in western areas around the capital <a href="/wiki/Conakry" title="Conakry">Conakry</a>, <a href="/wiki/For%C3%A9cariah" title="For√©cariah">For√©cariah</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kindia" title="Kindia">Kindia</a>. Smaller ethnic groups make up the remaining 16%<sup id="cite_ref-cia.gov_113-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia.gov-113">[113]</a></sup> of the population, including <a href="/wiki/Kpelle_people" title="Kpelle people">Kpelle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kissi_people" title="Kissi people">Kissi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zialo" class="mw-redirect" title="Zialo">Zialo</a>, Toma and others.<sup id="cite_ref-guinea_stats_12-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guinea_stats-12">[12]</a></sup> Approximately 10,000 non-Africans live in Guinea, predominantly Lebanese, French, and other Europeans.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Guinea" title="Religion in Guinea">Religion in Guinea</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="barbox tright" style="overflow-x: auto;"> 
       <div style="border:1px solid silver; font-size:88%; padding:0.4em; width:auto; background: white;"> 
        <table style="text-align:left; border-collapse:collapse; width:100%;"> 
         <tbody>
          <tr style="background:#ddd">

          </tr> 
          <tr style="font-size:88%; height:4px;"> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding:0 4px; text-align:left;"><b>Religion</b></td> 
           <td style="width:100px; text-align:left;"></td>

          </tr>

            <div style="background:lightgreen; width:85%; overflow: hidden;">

            <div style="background:brown; width:7%; overflow: hidden;">
             ‚Äâ

          </tr> 
         </tbody>
        </table> 
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Conakrymosque.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Conakrymosque.jpg/200px-Conakrymosque.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="267" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Conakrymosque.jpg/300px-Conakrymosque.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Conakrymosque.jpg/400px-Conakrymosque.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1944" data-file-height="2592"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Conakrymosque.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Conakry_Grand_Mosque" class="mw-redirect" title="Conakry Grand Mosque">Conakry Grand Mosque</a> in Guinea, one of the largest mosques in West Africa
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The population of Guinea is approximately 85 percent <a href="/wiki/Muslim" class="mw-redirect" title="Muslim">Muslim</a> and 8 percent <a href="/wiki/Christians" title="Christians">Christian</a>, with 7 percent adhering to indigenous religious beliefs.<sup id="cite_ref-state.gov_115-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-state.gov-115">[115]</a></sup> Much of the population, both Muslim and Christian, also incorporate indigenous African beliefs into their outlook.<sup id="cite_ref-state.gov_115-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-state.gov-115">[115]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The vast majority of Guinean <a href="/wiki/Muslims" title="Muslims">Muslims</a> are adherent to the <a href="/wiki/Sunni_Islam" title="Sunni Islam">Sunni</a> tradition of <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a>, of <a href="/wiki/Maliki" title="Maliki">Maliki</a> school of jurisprudence, influenced with <a href="/wiki/Sufism" title="Sufism">Sufism</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> There is also a <a href="/wiki/Shi%27a_Islam" class="mw-redirect" title="Shi'a Islam">Shi'a</a> community in Guinea. </p>
      <p>Christian groups include <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholics" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholics">Roman Catholics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anglicanism" title="Anglicanism">Anglicans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Baptists" title="Baptists">Baptists</a>, <a href="/wiki/Seventh-day_Adventist_Church" title="Seventh-day Adventist Church">Seventh-day Adventists</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Evangelicalism" title="Evangelicalism">Evangelical</a> groups. <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses" title="Jehovah's Witnesses">Jehovah's Witnesses</a> are active in the country and recognized by the Government. There is a small <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%CA%BC%C3%AD_Faith" title="Bah√° º√≠ Faith">Bah√° º√≠ Faith</a> community. There are small numbers of <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hindus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhists</a>, and traditional Chinese religious groups among the <a href="/wiki/Expatriate" title="Expatriate">expatriate</a> community.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>There were three days of ethno-religious fighting in the city of <a href="/wiki/Nzerekore" class="mw-redirect" title="Nzerekore">Nzerekore</a> in July 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-Guinea_2013_51-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guinea_2013-51">[51]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bbc.com_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc.com-118">[118]</a></sup> Fighting between ethnic <a href="/wiki/Kpelle_people" title="Kpelle people">Kpelle</a>, who are Christian or animist, and ethnic Konianke, who are Muslims and close to the larger <a href="/wiki/Malinke" class="mw-redirect" title="Malinke">Malinke</a> ethnic group, left at least 54 dead.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc.com_118-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc.com-118">[118]</a></sup> The dead included people who were killed with machetes and burned alive.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc.com_118-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc.com-118">[118]</a></sup> The violence ended after the Guinea military imposed a curfew, and President Conde made a televised appeal for calm.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc.com_118-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc.com-118">[118]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Guinea" title="Education in Guinea">Education in Guinea</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Guinea_schoolgirls.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Guinea_schoolgirls.jpg/220px-Guinea_schoolgirls.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="215" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Guinea_schoolgirls.jpg/330px-Guinea_schoolgirls.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Guinea_schoolgirls.jpg/440px-Guinea_schoolgirls.jpg 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="489"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Guinea_schoolgirls.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Schoolgirls in <a href="/wiki/Conakry" title="Conakry">Conakry</a>, Guinea
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The literacy rate of Guinea is one of the lowest in the world: in 2010 it was estimated that only 41% of adults were literate (52% of males and 30% of females).<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> Primary education is compulsory for 6 years,<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> but most children do not attend for so long, and many do not go to school at all. In 1999, primary school attendance was 40 percent. Children, particularly girls, are kept out of school to assist their parents with domestic work or agriculture,<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> or to be married: Guinea has one of the highest rates of <a href="/wiki/Child_marriage" title="Child marriage">child marriage</a> in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Health_in_Guinea" title="Health in Guinea">Health in Guinea</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ebola">Ebola</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Ebola">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Ebola_virus_epidemic_in_West_Africa" class="mw-redirect" title="Ebola virus epidemic in West Africa">Ebola virus epidemic in West Africa</a>
      </div> 
      <p>In 2014, there was an outbreak of the <a href="/wiki/Ebola_virus_epidemic_in_Guinea" title="Ebola virus epidemic in Guinea">Ebola virus in Guinea</a>. In response, the health ministry banned <a href="/wiki/Bushmeat" title="Bushmeat">the sale and consumption of bats</a>, thought to be carriers of the disease. Despite this measure, the virus eventually spread from rural areas to <a href="/wiki/Conakry" title="Conakry">Conakry</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> and by late June 2014 had spread to neighboring countries <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Leone" title="Sierra Leone">Sierra Leone</a> and <a href="/wiki/Liberia" title="Liberia">Liberia</a>. In early August 2014 Guinea closed its borders to Sierra Leone and Liberia to help contain the spreading of the virus, as more new cases of the disease were being reported in those countries than in Guinea. </p>
      <p>The outbreak began in early December, in a village called Meliandou, southeastern Guinea, not far from the borders with both Liberia and Sierra Leone. The first known case was a two-year-old child who died, after fever and vomiting and passing black stool, on 6 December. The child's mother died a week later, then a sister and a grandmother, all with symptoms that included fever, vomiting, and diarrhea. Then, by way of caregiving visits or attendance at funerals, the outbreak spread to other villages. </p>
      <p>Unsafe burials remained one of the primary sources of the transmission of the disease. The World Health Organization (WHO) reported that the inability to engage with local communities hindered the ability of health workers to trace the origins and strains of the virus.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>While WHO terminated the Public Health Emergency of International Concern (PHEIC) on 29 March 2016,<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> the Ebola Situation Report released on 30 March confirmed 5 more cases in the preceding two weeks, with viral sequencing relating one of the cases to the November 2014 outbreak.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The epidemic also affected the treatment of other diseases in Guinea. There was a decline in healthcare visits by the population due to fear of being infected and mistrust in the health care system, and a decrease in the system's ability to provide routine health care and HIV/AIDS treatments due to the Ebola outbreak.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Maternal_and_child_healthcare">Maternal and child healthcare</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Maternal and child healthcare">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The 2010 maternal mortality rate per 100,000 births for Guinea is 680. This is compared with 859.9 in 2008 and 964.7 in 1990. The under 5 mortality rate, per 1,000 births is 146 and the neonatal mortality as a percentage of under 5's mortality is 29. In Guinea the number of midwives per 1,000 live births is 1 and the lifetime risk of death for pregnant women is 1 in 26.<sup id="cite_ref-SOWMY_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SOWMY-128">[128]</a></sup> Guinea has the second highest prevalence of <a href="/wiki/Female_genital_mutilation" title="Female genital mutilation">female genital mutilation</a> in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span id="HIV.2FAIDS"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="HIV/AIDS">HIV/AIDS</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: HIV/AIDS">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/HIV/AIDS_in_Guinea" title="HIV/AIDS in Guinea">HIV/AIDS in Guinea</a>
      </div> 
      <p>An estimated 170,000 adults and children were infected at the end of 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup> Surveillance surveys conducted in 2001 and 2002 show higher rates of HIV in urban areas than in rural areas. Prevalence was highest in <a href="/wiki/Conakry" title="Conakry">Conakry</a> (5%) and in the cities of the <a href="/wiki/Forest_Guinea" class="mw-redirect" title="Forest Guinea">Forest Guinea</a> region (7%) bordering <a href="/wiki/C%C3%B4te_d%E2%80%99Ivoire" class="mw-redirect" title="C√¥te d‚ÄôIvoire">C√¥te d‚ÄôIvoire</a>, <a href="/wiki/Liberia" title="Liberia">Liberia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Leone" title="Sierra Leone">Sierra Leone</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-usaid_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-usaid-133">[133]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>HIV is spread primarily through multiple-partner heterosexual intercourse. Men and women are at nearly equal risk for HIV, with young people aged 15 to 24 most vulnerable. Surveillance figures from 2001 to 2002 show high rates among commercial sex workers (42%), active military personnel (6.6%), truck drivers and bush taxi drivers (7.3%), miners (4.7%), and adults with tuberculosis (8.6%).<sup id="cite_ref-usaid_133-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-usaid-133">[133]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Several factors are fueling the HIV/AIDS epidemic in Guinea. They include unprotected sex, multiple sexual partners, illiteracy, endemic poverty, unstable borders, refugee migration, lack of civic responsibility, and scarce medical care and public services.<sup id="cite_ref-usaid_133-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-usaid-133">[133]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Malnutrition">Malnutrition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Malnutrition">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Malnutrition" title="Malnutrition">Malnutrition</a> is a serious problem for Guinea. A 2012 study reported high chronic malnutrition rates, with levels ranging from 34% to 40% by region, as well as acute malnutrition rates above 10% in Upper Guinea's mining zones. The survey showed that 139,200 children suffer from acute malnutrition, 609,696 from chronic malnutrition and further 1,592,892 suffer from anemia. Degradation of care practices, limited access to medical services, inadequate hygiene practices and a lack of food diversity explain these levels.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Malaria">Malaria</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Malaria">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Malaria" title="Malaria">Malaria</a> is prevalent in Guinea. It is transmitted year-round, with peak transmission from July through October.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup> Malaria is one of the top causes of disability in Guinea.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="COVID-19_pandemic">COVID-19 pandemic</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: COVID-19 pandemic">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic_in_Guinea" title="COVID-19 pandemic in Guinea">COVID-19 pandemic in Guinea</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The first case of <a href="/wiki/COVID-19" class="mw-redirect" title="COVID-19">COVID-19</a> was reported in Guinea on 13 March <a href="/wiki/2020_in_Guinea" title="2020 in Guinea">2020</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-First_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-First-137">[137]</a></sup> By the end of 2020 the total number of confirmed cases was 13,722. Of these, 13,141 had recovered, 500 were active, and 81 people had died.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Guinea_Dinguiraye_market.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Guinea_Dinguiraye_market.jpg/300px-Guinea_Dinguiraye_market.jpg" decoding="async" width="300" height="195" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/77/Guinea_Dinguiraye_market.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="450" data-file-height="293"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Guinea_Dinguiraye_market.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A market stall selling vegetables in <a href="/wiki/Dinguiraye_Prefecture" title="Dinguiraye Prefecture">Dinguiraye Prefecture</a>, Guinea
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p><b><a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">Football</a></b> is the most popular sport in the country of <b>Guinea</b>.<sup id="cite_ref-Encyclopedia_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclopedia-139">[139]</a></sup> It is run by the <a href="/wiki/Guinean_Football_Federation" title="Guinean Football Federation">Guinean Football Federation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup> The association administers the <a href="/wiki/Guinea_national_football_team" title="Guinea national football team">national football team</a>, as well as the national league.<sup id="cite_ref-Encyclopedia_139-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclopedia-139">[139]</a></sup> It was founded in 1960 and affiliated with <a href="/wiki/FIFA" title="FIFA">FIFA</a> since 1962<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup> and with the <a href="/wiki/Confederation_of_African_Football" title="Confederation of African Football">Confederation of African Football</a> since 1963.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Guinea_national_football_team" title="Guinea national football team">Guinea national football team</a>, nicknamed <i>Syli nationale</i> (National Elephants), have played international football since 1962.<sup id="cite_ref-Encyclopedia_139-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclopedia-139">[139]</a></sup> Their first opponent was East Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-Encyclopedia_139-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclopedia-139">[139]</a></sup> They have yet to reach <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup" title="FIFA World Cup">World Cup</a> finals, but they were runners-up to Morocco in the <a href="/wiki/Africa_Cup_of_Nations" title="Africa Cup of Nations">Africa Cup of Nations</a> in 1976.<sup id="cite_ref-Encyclopedia_139-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclopedia-139">[139]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Guin%C3%A9e_Championnat_National" title="Guin√©e Championnat National">Guin√©e Championnat National</a> is the top division of Guinean football. Since it was established in 1965, three teams have dominated in winning the <a href="/wiki/Guin%C3%A9e_Coupe_Nationale" title="Guin√©e Coupe Nationale">Guin√©e Coupe Nationale</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-RSSSF_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RSSSF-143">[143]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Horoya_AC" title="Horoya AC">Horoya AC</a> leads with 16 titles and is the current (2017‚Äì2018) champion. <a href="/wiki/Hafia_FC" title="Hafia FC">Hafia FC</a> (known as Conakry II in 1960s) is second with 15 titles having dominated in 1960s and 70s, but the last coming in 1985. Third with 13 is <a href="/wiki/AS_Kaloum_Star" title="AS Kaloum Star">AS Kaloum Star</a>, known as Conakry I in the 1960s. All three teams are based in the capital, <a href="/wiki/Conakry" title="Conakry">Conakry</a>. No other team has more than five titles. </p>
      <p>The 1970s were a golden decade for Guinean football. Hafia FC won the <a href="/wiki/African_Cup_of_Champions_Clubs" class="mw-redirect" title="African Cup of Champions Clubs">African Cup of Champions Clubs</a> three times, in <a href="/wiki/1972_African_Cup_of_Champions_Clubs" title="1972 African Cup of Champions Clubs">1972</a>, <a href="/wiki/1975_African_Cup_of_Champions_Clubs" title="1975 African Cup of Champions Clubs">1975</a> and <a href="/wiki/1977_African_Cup_of_Champions_Clubs" title="1977 African Cup of Champions Clubs">1977</a>, while Horoya AC won the <a href="/wiki/1978_African_Cup_Winners%27_Cup" title="1978 African Cup Winners' Cup">1978 African Cup Winners' Cup</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Polygamy">Polygamy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Polygamy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Polygamy_in_Guinea" title="Polygamy in Guinea">Polygamy in Guinea</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Polygamy is generally prohibited by law in Guinea, but there are exceptions.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/UNICEF" title="UNICEF">UNICEF</a> reports that 53.4% of Guinean women aged 15‚Äì49 are in polygamous marriages.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Guinea" title="Music of Guinea">Music of Guinea</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Like other West African countries, Guinea has a rich musical tradition. The group <a href="/wiki/Bembeya_Jazz" class="mw-redirect" title="Bembeya Jazz">Bembeya Jazz</a> became popular in the 1960s after Guinean independence. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Cuisine_of_Guinea" title="Cuisine of Guinea">Cuisine of Guinea</a>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Guinean_cuisine" class="mw-redirect" title="Guinean cuisine">Guinean cuisine</a> varies by region with rice as the most common staple. Cassava is also widely consumed.<sup id="cite_ref-friends_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-friends-147">[147]</a></sup> Part of <a href="/wiki/West_African_cuisine" title="West African cuisine">West African cuisine</a>, the foods of Guinea include <a href="/wiki/Jollof_rice" title="Jollof rice">jollof rice</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maafe" class="mw-redirect" title="Maafe">maafe</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tapalapa_bread" title="Tapalapa bread">tapalapa bread</a>. In rural areas, food is eaten from a large serving dish and eaten by hand outside of homes.<sup id="cite_ref-dc_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dc-148">[148]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
